## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillations (ODE modeling of forced/damped oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of time t and velocity v, which is typical for reduced or phenomenological models of damped/forced nonlinear oscillators where acceleration includes damping terms in v and external/parametric forcing terms in t. With only (t, v) available, classical structures emphasize velocity-dependent dissipation and time-periodic drives rather than conservative restoring forces (which normally require displacement).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Free particle / zero-acceleration baseline: dv_dt = c0 (constant bias or sensor offset)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (exponential decay/growth of v depending on sign of c0)
- Quadratic drag (aerodynamic-like): dv_dt = c0 * v * Abs(v) (dissipation growing with speed; direction opposes v if c0<0)
- Cubic (odd) nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (weakly nonlinear dissipation/amplification near equilibrium)
- Higher-order odd damping series: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * v**5 (phenomenological friction law capturing strong nonlinearity)
- Dry/Coulomb friction model: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sign(v) (viscous plus approximately constant-magnitude friction)
- Stribeck-like friction (smooth dry friction): dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * tanh(c2 * v) (smooth transition through v=0, avoids discontinuity)
- Time-harmonic forcing (additive drive): dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3) (forced damped dynamics; drive independent of v)
- Multi-harmonic forcing: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t) + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (non-sinusoidal periodic drive approximation)
- Parametric modulation of damping: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * v (time-varying dissipation, e.g., parametrically driven damper)
- Velocity-dependent gain with periodic modulation: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * v + c3 * v**3 (parametric effects plus nonlinear damping)
- Relaxation/drive with exponential transient: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * exp(c2 * t) + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (start-up transient plus periodic forcing)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd symmetry in v (terms like v, v**3, v**5) often indicates friction/damping laws that reverse sign with velocity and dissipate energy when coefficients are negative.
- Terms using v*Abs(v) signal drag-like dissipation that grows ~|v|^2 and dominates at high speeds, typical of turbulent/aerodynamic resistance.
- Discontinuous or near-discontinuous behavior at v=0 (sign(v) or tanh(c*v)) reflects dry friction/stiction effects and can create stick–slip dynamics.
- Pure t-periodic additive terms (sin(c*t), cos(c*t)) represent external forcing; multiple harmonics suggest a nonsinusoidal drive waveform.
- Multiplying v by a periodic function of t, (c0 + c1*sin(c2*t))*v, is a hallmark of parametric modulation (time-varying damping/gain) and can induce instability bands.
- Presence of a constant bias term c0 (independent of t and v) can represent constant acceleration offset (e.g., tilt, gravity component, or measurement bias).
- Exponential-in-time transients exp(c*t) in dv_dt commonly indicate non-steady start-up/relaxation of the actuation or environment rather than intrinsic oscillator physics.
- Strong nonlinearity may appear as higher odd powers of v dominating at large |v|, producing amplitude-dependent decay rates and non-exponential relaxation of v(t).

\[
f(t,v)=0.782414626093252\,\sin(t)\;-\;0.0834249779987997\,v^3\;-\;0.995417005601056\,\log(|v|+1).
\]
So any matching candidate must be able (by choosing its free constants) to produce **exactly**:
- one pure sinusoid in \(t\) with no other \(t\)-dependence,
- a \(-0.0834\ldots v^3\) term,
- a \(-0.9954\ldots \log(|v|+1)\) term,
- and **no extra terms** (constants, \(v\), rational terms, exponentials, extra logs, etc.), unless their coefficients can be set to 0.

Also note: candidates use \(\log(c4|v|+1)\). To match \(\log(|v|+1)\) globally, we must set \(c4=1\). (You cannot compensate \(\log(a|v|+1)\) into \(\log(|v|+1)\) by scaling, since \(\log(a|v|+1)\neq \log(|v|+1)+\text{const}\) for all \(v\).)

Trigonometric matching: \(c0\sin(c1 t+c2)\) can match \(0.7824\sin(t)\) by setting \(c1=1\), \(c2=0\) (or \(c2=2\pi k\)), \(c0=0.7824\). (Other phase choices like \(c2=\pi\) would flip sign and require \(c0\) negative; also fine.)
